We all do business with different companies throughout the year and most are unremarkable. But our experience with General Manager, Adam Van Coops, at Redwood City Land Rover was extraordinary.
Adam‚Äôs communication, attention to detail and management skill is unsurpassed in the auto dealership industry; his overall customer service harkens back to an era of where a handshake meant he stood behind his products and service.
Our issue was the poor design in the tailgate operation of our Range Rover Sport; the tailgate would not fully open upon request and with a toddler in tow getting in and out of the trunk area was frustrating to say the least. We had to repeatedly activate the tailgate release (2-3 times) before it would fully open. It was serviced under warranty several times at Redwood City Land Rover without much success.
It wasn‚Äôt until we made contact with Adam that our frustration subsided and our appreciation for Redwood City Land Rover grew as the tailgate was serviced. Within a few short days, the tailgate was fully operational to factory specifications and returned to our family with a complete detail, which was much appreciated in the COVID-19 era. From the moment we discussed our issue with Adam, the poor car dealership stigma eroded and a professional business relationship emerged.
Our family will highly recommend Redwood City Land Rover to our friends and family. And without a doubt, our next SUV purchase will be at Redwood City Land Rover and with Adam Van Coops.< /review>

<review>I called about a car on November 15th, and was told it was available and for sale. I asked the salesman for some videos and more pictures, and he obliged. We had a short bargaining process, and agreed upon a price within several hundred dollars of their asking price. After this, we sent the funds in full (on the 17th) to the dealer, along with an email asking them to reply with confirmation that the car was sold and my shipper would pick up the car as soon as the funds cleared.

We received the contract from them with the buyers name being incorrect, along with the closing date being 1 month after the scheduled closing date AFTER we had corrected this over email prior to them sending the contract. They overnighted a new contract, and we signed and overnighted it back to them.

The dealer declined our original wire, and we were only notified after calling the dealership 5 times in order to reach the account manager, and we agreed to re wire the funds the same day. This took place on Friday the 20th, and they had the funds in their account on Monday morning at 6:30am.
I receive a call around 2pm on monday stating that "they are terribly sorry, but the car has been sold to a local buyer". Keep in mind this is AFTER we have a signed contract, and AFTER we have made a second attempt to wire the funds.

We escalated the matter to Adam, their GM who was very honest and upfront in what had happened. He did make us whole again, however after receiving the second check for the funds from them (the first check had the incorrect name), the funds will not be available in our account for 2 weeks from today.

I have purchased multiple cars out of state and am in sales myself. This was honestly was one of the worst transactions I have ever had, and the lack of professionalism from the dealer is astounding. Needed to get some scooter tires mounted to a set of rims. Looked all over and no one would do it. I tried doing it myself and failed miserably. At that point I was willing to pay what ever it cost to have it done. I remembered this place and looked it up. Reviews were decent and I had met Jason years ago so decided to give them a try. Jeremy was the mechanic that I was in contact with. Friendly, understanding he and he took care of my issue. They will definitely be my first call if I need anything else. He did tell me that they don't usually work on scooters or Vespas as their parts are difficult to find but on a case by case issue they might be able to help. That is better than most places and an honest answer. Keep up the good work guys!!< /Review>

< Review>
The Good: I am so happy that I joined SDRC last year. The monthly dues for membership and coaching are reasonable, you have 24/7 access to the boat house unless there's a special event, Coach Sean is really knowledgeable and helpful, and I've met a lot of awesome people here. Mid-weight racing sculls are often in use, so it's good that they allow you to reserve boats for free in advance. As a member, you'll also be able to attend their extravagant galas and informational seminars.

The Bad: I have had a few unpleasant encounters with grouches who almost put me off of joining SDRC, but I would say that the majority of members are friendly.</Review>

<Rating>1< /Rating>< Review>
Reasonable price for Korean BBQ, ranging from 12-20$. Children 4-9 in age get a discount. The restaurant didn't have smoke vents on top of each table which made it stink of smoke. They had a buffet looking bar that served fruits and other starters. The fruit looked and tasted like it's been there for a while and the kimchi rots and is very sour. I ordered a few orders of meat which made me loose my appetite after a few bites. The service is really poor. I asked for my grill to be changed but the servant gave me a big fat "NO". After the denied request came servants consistently lowering my fire. The meat tasted bland, dry, and cheap. People who would say this is a great restaurant haven't tried real Korean BBQ. Would I come back? No I wouldn't.< /Review>

$12 for AYCE.  It's Chinese owned. Only 2 employees at any given time so it's mostly self service but for meats.  Good value, but leaves a lot to be desired.  Little things like incorrect silverware and utensils for Korean food.  Those things bug me.   For the same price, Red Castle chains are much much better.  My one complaint is the restaurant feels dirty.  The sides of the grills aren't properly cleaned so there is residual splatter from prior patrons.  The floors are also pretty slippery.  That being said, we go there at least once a month.   Cheapest place in town.</Review>

< Review>
The store Manager (Chris) is miles apart better than the store Manager at the Tustin Games Workshop. Chris is obviously well versed in all of the products, history, culture, and fluff of each army and game. He gets to know the customers, remembers key info (he doesn't act like hes never met you each time you walk into his store). The gamers are well behaved and organized, the store is always picked up and clean, the product is always organized and Chris knows every detail of every model. Doesn't push the sale but his enthusiasm certainly makes you want to buy.< /Review>
